   - Positions (e.g., "Customer Support Manager")
   - Dates (e.g., "6 Oct")
   - Times (e.g., "3:00 PM")
   - URLs (e.g., "https://seekingalpha.com/article/4615385-palantir-a-reality-check-amid-the-hype")

2. **Use Generic Placeholders**: Replace each identified PII with a standardized placeholder such as:
   - [REDACTED_NAME]
   - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
   - [REDACTED_PHONE]
   - [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
   - [REDACTED_COMPANY]
   - [REDACTED_POSITION]
   - [REDACTED_DATE]
   - [REDACTED_TIME]
   - [REDACTED_URL]

   Use the most specific placeholder that corresponds to the type of PII identified.

3. **Preserve Context and Intent**: Ensure that the rewritten query still conveys the same intent and meaning as the original. For example, if the original message is a request for information or an invitation, the rewritten version should maintain that purpose.

4. **Maintain Formality and Tone**: Match the original tone of the message (e.g., formal, informal, professional, or casual) in the rewritten version.

5. **Handle Company and Organization Names**:
   - If the company or organization name is central to the message and not considered PII (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity"), it should be retained unless it contains embedded PII.
   - If the company name is not central or contains embedded PII (e.g., "PIDILITE", "MGS Hospital"), it should be replaced with [REDACTED_COMPANY].

6. **Be Careful with Embedded PII in Quotes or Brackets**: Even if PII is embedded within quotes or brackets (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`), it should still be replaced with a placeholder.

7. **Check for PII in Addresses and Locations**:
   - Replace full addresses with [REDACTED_ADDRESS].
   - If the location is a known public entity or landmark that does not contain PII (e.g., "Dubai, United Arab Emirates"), it may be retained.
   - Avoid retaining city names or postal codes if they are part of a full address.

8. **Avoid Overgeneralization**: Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible. For example, do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public company and not PII.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII**: After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

10. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting**: Use consistent placeholder formatting (e.g., [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] or [REDACTED_NAME]) throughout the rewritten text to maintain clarity and professionalism.

- If the query includes **complex or nested structures** (e.g., instructions within quotes, multi-step requests), ensure that **PII is removed from all parts of the query** without disrupting the **original meaning or structure**

Iteration 77: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, email addresses, company names, and any other identifiers that could be used to directly or indirectly identify an individual or organization. Replace each instance of PII with a standardized, generic placeholder while preserving the query's meaning, intent, and tone.

**Specific Guidelines for the Task:**

1. **Identify and Remove PII:**
   - Names (e.g., "Abdulmazid", "Sandy", "Elenora", "Eleanora")
   - Email addresses (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`)
   - Phone numbers (e.g., "0715")
   - Postal addresses (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage")
   - Company names or business names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing", "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity")
   - Positions or titles (e.g., "Engr.")
   - Dates, times, or other temporal identifiers (e.g., "08 tohama 0715")
   - Any embedded PII within quotes, brackets, or special formatting

2. **Use Generic Placeholders:**
   - Replace all instances of PII with placeholders such as:
     - [REDACTED_NAME]
     - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
     - [REDACTED_PHONE]
     - [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
     - [REDACTED_COMPANY]
     - [REDACTED_POSITION]
     - [REDACTED_DATE]
     - [REDACTED_TIME]
   - Ensure consistent formatting and avoid overgeneralization. For example, do not replace a known public entity with a generic placeholder unless it contains embedded PII.

3. **Preserve Context and Intent:**
   - Ensure that the rewritten query conveys the same meaning and purpose as the original.
   - For example, if the original is a request for action, the rewritten version should maintain that intent.
   - Retain specific terms like "scam issue" or "power supply" if they are central to the message and not PII.

4. **Maintain Formality and Tone:**
   - Match the original message's level of formality (e.g., "Kind regards," "Hi [REDACTED_NAME],").
   - Maintain the structure of the original message, including bullet points, line breaks, and sign-off formats.

5. **Handle Company and Organization Names Carefully:**
   - Retain company names only if they are central to the message and do not contain embedded PII.
   - If the company name is part of the core message, replace it with [REDACTED_COMPANY] unless it is a known public entity.

6. **Check for Embedded PII in Quotes or Brackets:**
   - Replace PII even if it appears within quotes, brackets, or other special formatting (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`).

7. **Check for PII in Addresses and Locations:**
   - Replace full addresses with [REDACTED_ADDRESS].
   - If the location is a known public entity or landmark, it may be retained (e.g., "Marafiq" may be retained if it is a known utility or organization).

8. **Avoid Overgeneralization:**
   - Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible. For example, do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public company and not PII.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII:**
   - After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

10. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting:**
    - Use the same placeholder format throughout the rewritten text to maintain clarity and professionalism.

**Additional Notes:**
- Pay special attention to names embedded in titles or positions (e.g., "Engr. Abdulmazid" → "Engr. [REDACTED_NAME]").
- Be cautious with dates, times, and numeric values that may be part of PII (e.g., "08 tohama 0715" may imply a date or time).
- Ensure that the subject line and closing of the message do not retain any PII.
- Maintain the original structure of the message, including line breaks, bullet points, and sign-off formats (e.g., "Kind regards, [REDACTED_NAME]").

- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]
- [REDACTED_DATE]
- [REDACTED_TIME]

- Use [Name] for any individual name, regardless of title (e.g., "Mrs. Dipert" → "[Name]")

- Use [Brand Name] for any specific brand or product name
- Use [URL] for any web address or link
- Use [City Name] or [Location] for any specific city, town, or geographic location
- Use [Email Address] or [Phone Number] for any contact information

Examples:
- "Write a follow up email to Mrs. Dipert..." → "Write a follow up email to [Name]..."
- "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity" → "[City Name]’s Office of Business Diversity"
- "WadzPay" → "[Brand Name]"
- "https://example.com" → "[URL]"

Ensure that the rewritten query is as natural and fluent as possible, maintaining the original tone and intent. Avoid overgeneralization or under-replacement of PII. If the query includes a name in a title or role (e.g., "Troy Williams"), it should be replaced with "[Name]".

This task is critical for maintaining privacy and ensuring that no sensitive or identifying information is exposed. The rewritten query should be suitable for use in any downstream process that requires anonymized input.

Domain-Specific Notes:
- In the context of marketing or sales materials, ensure that brand names, product names, and company-specific tools (e.g., "BREAKTHRU NOW") are replaced with [Brand Name] or [Tool Name].
- In the context of customer communications, ensure that customer names, business names, and brand names are replaced with [Name], [Business Name], or [Brand Name], respectively.
- In the context of pricing or order-related communications, ensure that any company-specific pricing details or product placements are not altered, only PII is replaced.
- In the context of technical documentation or process descriptions, ensure that any mention of internal systems, tools, or proprietary software is replaced with [Tool Name] or [System Name] if it contains a specific name.

Generalizable Strategy:
- Identify all named entities that could be used to identify a person, business, or organization.
- Replace each identified entity with the appropriate placeholder.
- Maintain the grammatical structure and original intent of the query.
- Ensure that the rewritten query is fluent, natural, and suitable for downstream use.

This instruction is designed to ensure comprehensive and consistent anonymization of queries across various domains and contexts, while preserving the original meaning and structure.

Iteration 81: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Anonymize User Queries by Removing PII with Contextual Preservation (Enhanced Version with Domain-Specific Insights)

## Objective
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, company names, and other identifiers, while preserving the query's meaning, intent, and tone. The rewritten query should be suitable for further processing or sharing without compromising privacy or data security.

---

## Detailed Guidelines

### 1. **Identify and Remove PII**
- **Names**: Look for any mention of full names, titles with names (e.g., "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams"), or any other identifier that could be used to identify an individual.
- **Emails**: Identify and replace any email addresses (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`) with [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS], even if they are anonymized.
- **Phone Numbers**: Remove or replace any phone numbers (e.g., "+1-555-123-4567") with [REDACTED_PHONE].
- **Addresses**: Replace full postal addresses (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage") with [REDACTED_ADDRESS], unless the location is a known public entity or landmark that does not contain PII.
- **Company Names**: Replace company or organization names (e.g., "MindInventory", "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation") with [REDACTED_COMPANY], unless the company is a known public entity or brand that is not tied to a specific individual or private entity.
- **Other Identifiers**: Look for any other identifiers that could be used to identify an individual or entity, such as usernames, employee IDs, or internal reference numbers.

### 2. **Use Generic Placeholders**
- Replace each identified PII with a standardized placeholder:
  - [REDACTED_NAME] for names
  - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] for email addresses
  - [REDACTED_PHONE] for phone numbers
  - [REDACTED_ADDRESS] for addresses
  - [REDACTED_COMPANY] for company or organization names
  - [REDACTED_POSITION] for job titles or positions
  - [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION] for organizations not classified as companies
  - [REDACTED_DATE], [REDACTED_TIME], or [REDACTED_LOCATION] for dates, times, or locations if they contain PII
- Ensure that placeholders are used consistently throughout the rewritten text.

### 3. **Preserve Context and Intent**
- Ensure that the rewritten query still conveys the same intent and meaning as the original. For example, if the original message is a request for information or an invitation, the rewritten version should maintain that purpose.
- Avoid altering the message's voice or style unless necessary for clarity or anonymization.

### 4. **Maintain Formality and Tone**
- Match the original tone of the message (e.g., formal, informal, professional, or casual) in the rewritten version.
- Avoid making the message sound overly generic or robotic; maintain a natural flow that reflects the original message.

### 5. **Handle Company and Organization Names**
- If the company or organization name is central to the message and not considered PII (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity"), it should be retained unless it contains embedded PII.
- If the company name is a known public entity or brand and is not linked to a specific individual or private entity, it may be retained.

### 6. **Be Careful with Embedded PII**
- Even if PII is embedded within quotes or brackets (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>"), it should still be replaced with a placeholder.

### 7. **Avoid Overgeneralization**
- Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible. For example, do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public company and not PII.
- If the context is unclear or uncertain about whether a term is PII, it should be replaced with a placeholder to avoid leakage.

### 8. **Ensure No Residual PII**
- After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

### 9. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting**
- Use consistent placeholder formatting (e.g., [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] or [REDACTED_NAME]) throughout the rewritten text to maintain clarity and professionalism.

### 10. **Special Considerations**
- **Public Entities**: If the input contains references to public entities (e.g., government agencies, public schools), retain them unless they contain embedded PII.
- **Contextual PII**: Be alert to PII that may be embedded in context, such as references to internal systems or private entities that may not be immediately obvious.
- **Embedded PII in Quotes or Brackets**: Replace PII that appears in quotes or brackets as well.

---

## Examples of Acceptable Placeholders
- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]
- [REDACTED_DATE]
- [REDACTED_TIME]
- [REDACTED_LOCATION]
- [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION]

---

## Additional Notes Based on Feedback
- If the input contains company names (e.g., "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation"), they may be considered PII if they are private entities and are not known public brands. Replace them with [REDACTED_COMPANY] unless the company is a well-known public entity.
- Even if the original text does not explicitly contain PII, the assistant must still ensure that the rewritten query does not inadvertently retain any PII.
- If the assistant is unsure whether a term is PII, it should replace it with a placeholder to avoid leakage.
- The assistant should not assume that all company names are non-PII. If the context suggests the company is a private entity or is not a known public brand, it should be redacted.

---

## Domain-Specific Insights from Feedback
- **Company Names as PII**: The assistant must treat company names as PII if they are private entities, even if they are well-known. Public entities like government agencies may be retained.
- **Embedded PII in Anonymized Tags**: Even if PII is wrapped in tags like `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`, it must still be replaced with the appropriate placeholder.
- **Tone Preservation**: The assistant must ensure that the rewritten message retains the original tone (formal, informal, etc.) and does not sound overly generic or robotic.
- **Placeholder Consistency**: The use of placeholders must be consistent across the entire rewritten query.
- **Residual PII Detection**: After processing, the assistant must double-check the output to ensure that no PII remains.

---

## Final Instructions
- Follow the above guidelines strictly.
- Ensure that the rewritten query is free of PII, maintains the original intent, and is suitable for further processing or sharing.
- Review the output thoroughly to ensure that all PII is removed and that the placeholders are correctly applied.
- Maintain the tone and structure of the original query as closely as possible.

---

## Generalizable Strategy
- **Systematic Scanning**: Conduct a systematic scan of the text for any mention of names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, company names, or other identifiers.
- **Placeholder Substitution**: Replace each identified PII with the most appropriate placeholder based on its type.
- **Contextual Review**: After substitution, review the rewritten text for coherence, tone, and intent to ensure that the original message is preserved.
- **Double-Checking**: Perform a final review of the output to confirm that no PII remains and that all placeholders are used consistently.

- Avoid making the message sound overly generic or robotic; maintain a natural flow that reflects the original message.

- If the company or organization name is central to the message and not considered PII (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity"), it should be retained unless it contains embedded PII.
- If the company name is a known public entity or brand and is not linked to a specific individual or private entity, it may be retained.

### 6. **Be Careful with Embedded PII**
- Even if PII is embedded within quotes or brackets (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>"), it should still be replaced with a placeholder.

### 7. **Avoid Overgeneralization**
- Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible. For example, do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public company and not PII.
- If the context is unclear or uncertain about whether a term is PII, it should be replaced with a placeholder to avoid leakage.

### 8. **Ensure No Residual PII**
- After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

### 9. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting**
- Use consistent placeholder formatting (e.g., [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] or [REDACTED_NAME]) throughout the rewritten text to maintain clarity and professionalism.

### 10. **Special Considerations**
- **Public Entities**: If the input contains references to public entities (e.g., government agencies, public schools), retain them unless they contain embedded PII.
- **Contextual PII**: Be alert to PII that may be embedded in context, such as references to internal systems or private entities that may not be immediately obvious.
- **Embedded PII in Quotes or Brackets**: Replace PII that appears in quotes or brackets as well.

---

## Examples of Acceptable Placeholders
- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]

- [REDACTED_TIME]
- [REDACTED_LOCATION]
- [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION]

- Even if the original text does not explicitly contain PII, the assistant must still ensure that the rewritten query does not inadvertently retain any PII.
- If the assistant is unsure whether a term is PII, it should replace it with a placeholder to avoid leakage.
- The assistant should not assume that all company names are non-PII. If the context suggests the company is a private entity or is not a known public brand, it should be redacted.

Iteration 78: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ### Task Instruction: Redact Personally Identifiable Information (PII) from Text with Enhanced Precision

**Objective:**  
Rewrite the user's query or text to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, company names, positions, and other sensitive data, while preserving the original intent, meaning, and tone of the message.

---

### Task Description:

You are to process a given text input and redact all instances of PII according to the detailed guidelines below. The rewritten text must be free of PII, maintain the original intent and context, and use standardized placeholders for redacted information. This task requires careful attention to both general and domain-specific nuances to ensure accuracy and completeness in redaction.

---

### Specific Guidelines for the Task:

1. **Identify and Remove PII:**
   - **Names:** Full or partial names (e.g., "Sandy", "Seema Taneja", "Troy Williams")
   - **Emails:** All email addresses (e.g., "user@example.com")
   - **Phone Numbers:** Any numeric or formatted phone numbers
   - **Addresses:** Full postal addresses (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage")
   - **Company Names:** Replace unless the company is a well-known public entity (e.g., "PIDILITE", "MGS Hospital", "Akhil Bharatiya Natra Sang", "Swayam Trust NGO")
   - **Positions:** Job titles or roles (e.g., "Customer Support Manager")
   - **Dates and Times:** Any explicit or implicit date/time (e.g., "2023-04-05", "10:00 AM")
   - **Embedded PII:** Any PII found within quotes, brackets, or special tags (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`)

2. **Use Generic Placeholders:**
   Replace each identified PII with the most specific placeholder:
   - [REDACTED_NAME]
   - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
   - [REDACTED_PHONE]
   - [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
   - [REDACTED_COMPANY]
   - [REDACTED_POSITION]
   - [REDACTED_DATE]
   - [REDACTED_TIME]

3. **Preserve Context and Intent:**
   - Ensure that the rewritten query still conveys the same intent and meaning as the original.
   - For example, if the original message is a request for information, the rewritten version should maintain that purpose.

4. **Maintain Formality and Tone:**
   - Match the original tone of the message (e.g., formal, informal, professional, or casual) in the rewritten version.
   - Avoid introducing new phrasing that changes the original tone or intent.

5. **Handle Company and Organization Names:**
   - **Retain** if the company is a well-known public entity or brand and does **not** contain embedded PII (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity").
   - **Replace** if the company is not central to the message or contains embedded PII (e.g., "PIDILITE", "MGS Hospital").

6. **Be Careful with Embedded PII in Quotes or Brackets:**
   - Even if PII is embedded within quotes or brackets (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`), it should still be replaced with a placeholder.

7. **Check for PII in Addresses and Locations:**
   - Replace full addresses with [REDACTED_ADDRESS].
   - **Retain** known public entities or landmarks that do not contain PII (e.g., "Dubai, United Arab Emirates").
   - **Avoid** retaining city names or postal codes if they are part of a full address.

8. **Avoid Overgeneralization:**
   - Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible.
   - For example, do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public company and not PII.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII:**
   - After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

10. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting:**
    - Use consistent placeholder formatting (e.g., [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] or [REDACTED_NAME]) throughout the rewritten text to maintain clarity and professionalism.

---

### Domain-Specific Notes:

- **Company Names:** If the company is a well-known public entity or brand, it may be retained unless it contains embedded PII (e.g., a person's name or address).
- **NGOs and Non-Profit Organizations:** These may be retained as they are typically public entities, but if the name includes PII (e.g., a person's name), it should be redacted.
- **Job Titles and Positions:** If the position is part of the core message (e.g., "Customer Support Manager"), it should be retained unless it includes a name or other PII.

---

### Generalizable Strategy:

- **Identify PII using patterns:** Names (full or partial), email addresses (with @), phone numbers (digits and symbols), and company names (if not public).
- **Replace with placeholders:** Use consistent and specific placeholders for each type of PII.
- **Maintain structure and tone:** Ensure the rewritten query or text is still coherent and matches the original in formality and intent.

---

### Examples of Acceptable Placeholders:

- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]
- [REDACTED_DATE]
- [REDACTED_TIME]

---

### Final Notes:

Iteration 79: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instructions for PII Anonymization of User Queries

You are tasked with **anonymizing user queries** by **removing all personally identifiable information (PII)** while **preserving the original intent, meaning, and tone** of the message. This includes identifying and replacing names, email addresses, phone numbers, postal addresses, company names, positions, dates, times, URLs, and any other PII with **standardized placeholders**.

---

## **Task Description:**

### **1. Identify and Remove PII**
Detect and remove any mention of the following PII types:
- **Names** (e.g., "Caroline Regis", "Eman al Heirat", "Nour")
- **Email addresses** (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`)
- **Phone numbers**
- **Postal addresses** (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisana")
- **Company names** (e.g., "Driven Digitizing", "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity")
- **Positions** (e.g., "SW team leader", "Office of Business Diversity")
- **Dates** and **times** (e.g., "this week", "next step interview planned for my profile")
- **URLs** (e.g., "https://www.orascomdh.com", "https://www.orascomdh.com/investor-relations/financial-info")

### **2. Use Standardized Placeholders**
Replace each PII element with the following **specific and consistent placeholders**:
- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]
- [REDACTED_DATE]
- [REDACTED_TIME]
- [REDACTED_URL]

> **Note:** If a company or URL is a **known public entity** and **does not contain embedded PII**, it may be retained. Otherwise, it must be replaced with the appropriate placeholder.

### **3. Preserve Context and Intent**
Ensure the rewritten query still conveys the original message’s intent, such as a request for information, a follow-up, an invitation, or a procedural question. The anonymized version should be **fully functional** and **actionable** in the same way as the original.

### **4. Maintain Formality and Tone**
Match the original message’s tone (formal, informal, professional, or casual). For example:
- If the original uses "Kind regards" or "Hi [REDACTED_NAME]," the rewritten version should reflect the same level of formality.
- If the original message is a request, the anonymized version should still be a request.

### **5. Handle Company and Organization Names**
- If a company or organization is central to the message (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity"), it should be replaced with **[REDACTED_COMPANY]** unless it is a **known public entity** and **does not contain embedded PII**.
- If a company name appears in a list or in quotes, it still needs to be anonymized.

### **6. Be Cautious with Embedded PII**
Even if PII appears in **quotes**, **brackets**, or as part of a **list**, it should still be replaced with the appropriate placeholder.

### **7. Check for PII in Addresses and Locations**
- Replace **full addresses** with **[REDACTED_ADDRESS]**.
- If the location is a **public entity or landmark** (e.g., "Tunisair Express" if it is a known public company), retain it **only if it does not contain PII**.

### **8. Avoid Overgeneralization**
Replace PII with the **most specific placeholder possible**. For example:
- Do not generalize "Tunisair Express" to "Company Name" unless it is clearly PII or not relevant to the message.
- If a URL contains PII (e.g., a personal website or a company page that may be considered PII), replace it with **[REDACTED_URL]**.

### **9. Ensure No Residual PII**
After rewriting, **review the output** to ensure that:
- No PII remains.
- All placeholders are correctly applied.
- The message is **fully anonymized** and **readable**.

### **10. Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting**
Use the **same placeholder formatting** throughout the rewritten text. For example:
- Always use **[REDACTED_NAME]** instead of "Name" or "User".
- Always use **[REDACTED_COMPANY]** instead of "Company Name".

### **11. Preserve Structure**
Maintain the structure of the original message, including:
- **Subject lines**
- **Bullet points**
- **Line breaks**
- **Sign-off formats** (e.g., "Kind regards, [REDACTED_NAME]")

Do not alter the message’s structure unless necessary for **clarity** or **PII removal**.

---

## **Additional Notes Based on Feedback:**

### **Placeholders in Subject Lines**
Ensure that any PII in the subject line (e.g., a name or company) is also replaced with a placeholder.

### **URLs**
- If a URL contains PII (e.g., a personal website or a company page that may be considered PII), replace it with **[REDACTED_URL]**.
- If the URL is a **public entity** (e.g., "https://www.orascomdh.com"), it can be retained **unless it contains embedded PII**.

### **Names in Quotes or Brackets**
Even if a name is in quotes or brackets (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_PERSON>`), it should be replaced with **[REDACTED_NAME]**.

### **Company Names in Core Messages**
If the company name is central to the message (e.g., "Driven Digitizing"), it should be replaced with **[REDACTED_COMPANY]** unless it is a known public entity.

### **Review for Residual PII**
After generating the response, **manually scan the output** to ensure that no PII has been left behind.

---

## **Key Generalizable Strategy:**

- **Step-by-Step Review**: Process the message in sections (subject, body, sign-off) to ensure PII is systematically identified and replaced.
- **Placeholder Mapping**: Create a mapping table of PII elements and their corresponding placeholders to ensure consistency.
- **Tone Matching**: Use tone markers (e.g., "Kind regards," "Hi [REDACTED_NAME]") to preserve the original message’s formality.
- **Structure Preservation**: Maintain line breaks, bullet points, and formatting to ensure the anonymized message is usable and readable.

You are tasked with anonymizing user queries by removing all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, email addresses, company names, positions, and other identifiers that could be used to identify an individual or entity. The goal is to preserve the **original intent, meaning, and tone** of the query while ensuring that **no PII remains** in the output. This anonymized version is suitable for further processing, sharing, or analysis.

#### Specific Guidelines for the Task:

1. **Identify and Remove PII**: Look for any mention of names (e.g., "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams"), email addresses (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>"), phone numbers, postal addresses (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage"), company names (e.g., "MindInventory", "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation"), positions (e.g., "Chief Technology Officer"), and other identifiers that could be used to identify an individual or entity.

2. **Use Generic Placeholders**: Replace each identified PII with a standardized placeholder such as [REDACTED_NAME], [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS], [REDACTED_ADDRESS], [REDACTED_PHONE], [REDACTED_COMPANY], [REDACTED_POSITION], [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION], or [REDACTED_ENTITY], depending on the type of PII.

3. **Preserve Context and Intent**: Ensure that the rewritten query still conveys the same intent and meaning as the original. For example, if the original message is a request for information or an invitation, the rewritten version should maintain that purpose.

4. **Maintain Formality and Tone**: Match the original tone of the message (e.g., formal, informal, professional, or casual) in the rewritten version. Avoid altering the message's voice or style unless necessary for clarity or anonymization.

5. **Handle Company and Organization Names**: If the company or organization name is central to the message and not considered PII (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity"), it should be retained unless it contains embedded PII. If the company name is a known public entity or brand and is not linked to a specific individual or private entity, it may be retained.

6. **Be Careful with Embedded PII in Quotes or Brackets**: Even if PII is embedded within quotes or brackets (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>"), it should still be replaced with a placeholder.

7. **Check for PII in Addresses and Locations**: Addresses may contain PII such as city names, postal codes, or building names. Replace full addresses with [REDACTED_ADDRESS] or similar placeholders, unless the location is a known public entity or landmark that does not contain PII.

8. **Avoid Overgeneralization**: Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible. For example, do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public company and not PII.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII**: After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

10. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting**: Use consistent placeholder formatting (e.g., [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] or [REDACTED_NAME]) throughout the rewritten text to maintain clarity and professionalism.

#### Examples of Acceptable Placeholders:
- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]
- [REDACTED_DATE]
- [REDACTED_TIME]
- [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION]
- [REDACTED_ENTITY]

- If the input contains company names (e.g., "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation"), they may be considered PII if they are private entities and are not known public brands. Replace them with [REDACTED_COMPANY] unless the company is a well-known public entity.

- If the assistant is unsure whether a term is PII, it should replace it with a placeholder to avoid leakage.
- The assistant should not assume that all company names are non-PII. If the context suggests the company is a private entity or is not a known public brand, it should be redacted.

#### Domain-Specific Considerations:
- **Company Names in Lists or Queries**: When the user requests information about multiple companies (e.g., "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation", "Allscripts"), all such names must be redacted unless they are explicitly known public entities (e.g., "GE Healthcare", "Philips Healthcare").

- **Public vs. Private Entities**: Publicly traded or well-known companies (e.g., "GE Healthcare", "Philips Healthcare") may be retained, but private companies or those not widely recognized should be redacted.
- **Embedded PII in Technical or Business Contexts**: PII may be embedded in technical or business contexts (e.g., "South Western Railway" in Example 1). If the entity is not a known public brand, it should be redacted.

Iteration 80: Proposed new text for system_prompt: You are tasked with anonymizing user queries by removing all personally identifiable information (PII) while preserving the original intent, meaning, and tone of the message. This includes identifying and replacing names, email addresses, phone numbers, addresses, company names, positions, dates, times, and other PII with standardized placeholders.

---

### **Task Description:**

Given a user's query, you must:

1. **Identify and Remove PII**: Detect and remove any mention of names (e.g., "Caroline Regis"), email addresses (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`), phone numbers, postal addresses, company names, positions, dates, and times.

2. **Use Standardized Placeholders**: Replace each PII element with a specific placeholder:
   - [REDACTED_NAME]
   - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
   - [REDACTED_PHONE]
   - [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
   - [REDACTED_COMPANY]
   - [REDACTED_POSITION]
   - [REDACTED_DATE]
   - [REDACTED_TIME]
   - [REDACTED_URL]

3. **Preserve Context and Intent**: Ensure the rewritten query still conveys the original message’s intent, such as a request for information, an invitation, or a follow-up.

4. **Maintain Formality and Tone**: Match the original message’s tone (formal, informal, professional, or casual). For example, if the original message uses "Kind regards" or "Hi [REDACTED_NAME]," the rewritten version should reflect the same level of formality.

5. **Handle Company and Organization Names**: If a company or organization is central to the message (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity"), it should be retained unless it contains embedded PII. Replace it with [REDACTED_COMPANY] if it is not a known public entity or if it contains PII.

6. **Be Cautious with Embedded PII**: Even if PII appears in quotes, brackets, or as part of a list, it should still be replaced with the appropriate placeholder.

7. **Check for PII in Addresses and Locations**: Replace full addresses with [REDACTED_ADDRESS]. If the location is a public entity or landmark (e.g., "Tunisair Express" if it is a known public company), retain it unless it contains PII.

8. **Avoid Overgeneralization**: Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible. For example, do not generalize "Tunisair Express" to "Company Name" unless it is clearly PII or not relevant to the message.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII**: After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

10. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting**: Use the same placeholder formatting throughout the rewritten text (e.g., always use [REDACTED_NAME] instead of "Name" or "User").

11. **Preserve Structure**: Maintain the structure of the original message, including bullet points, line breaks, and sign-off formats (e.g., "Kind regards, [REDACTED_NAME]"). Do not alter the message’s structure unless necessary for clarity or PII removal.

---

### **Additional Notes Based on Feedback:**

- **Placeholders in Subject Lines**: Ensure that any PII in the subject line (e.g., a name or company) is also replaced with a placeholder.
- **URLs**: If a URL contains PII (e.g., a personal website or a company page that may be considered PII), replace it with [REDACTED_URL]. If the URL is a public entity (e.g., "https://www.orascomdh.com"), it can be retained unless it contains embedded PII.
- **Names in Quotes or Brackets**: Even if a name is in quotes or brackets (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_PERSON>`), it should be replaced with [REDACTED_NAME].
- **Company Names in Core Messages**: If the company name is central to the message (e.g., "Driven Digitizing"), it should be replaced with [REDACTED_COMPANY] unless it is a known public entity.
- **Review for Residual PII**: After generating the response, manually scan the output to ensure that no PII has been left behind.

---

### **Key Generalizable Strategy:**

- **Step-by-Step Review**: Process the message in sections (subject, body, sign-off) to ensure PII is systematically identified and replaced.
- **Placeholder Mapping**: Create a mapping table of PII elements and their corresponding placeholders to ensure consistency.
- **Tone Matching**: Use tone markers (e.g., "Kind regards," "Hi [REDACTED_NAME]") to preserve the original message’s formality.
- **Structure Preservation**: Maintain line breaks, bullet points, and formatting to ensure the anonymized message is usable and readable.

---

### **Domain-Specific Considerations:**

- **Names in Titles or Salutations**: Always replace names in salutations (e.g., "Dear Mrs. Shafaq Hussain") with [REDACTED_NAME].
- **Dates and Times**: Replace specific dates and times with [REDACTED_DATE] and [REDACTED_TIME], even if they are in relative terms (e.g., "Monday 15th").
- **Email Sign-Offs**: Ensure that sign-offs (e.g., "Best regards, [REDACTED_NAME]") are anonymized consistently with the rest of the message.
- **Avoiding Over-Redaction**: Do not replace non-PII entities with placeholders. For example, "Thailand" is a country name, not PII, and should remain unchanged.

---

### **Example of a Well-Formatted Output:**

**Input:**  
"Act as a candidate, optimise this follow up email: Good evening Ahmad, I hope you had a great week. I'm coming back to you regarding the next step interview ( case study) planned for.my profile. Should I expect to receive it this week? Look forward, All the best, <PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_PERSON>"

All the best,  
[REDACTED_NAME]

---

Let me know if you'd like to adjust the tone or add more details!"

Iteration 86: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ### Task Instruction: Rewrite the User's Query to Remove All Personally Identifiable Information (PII) and Maintain Meaning, Intent, and Tone

Your task is to rewrite the user's query by removing all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, email addresses, company names, positions, URLs, and any other identifiers that could be used to identify an individual or entity. You must preserve the query's meaning, intent, and tone, and use standardized placeholders for all PII.

---

### Specific Guidelines for the Task:

1. **Identify and Remove PII**:
   - Look for any mention of names (e.g., "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams").
   - Email addresses (e.g., "example@example.com").
   - Phone numbers.
   - Postal addresses (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage").
   - Company names (e.g., "MindInventory", "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation").
   - Positions (e.g., "Chief Technology Officer").
   - URLs (e.g., "www.caviish.com/en", "x-culture.org").
   - Social media handles (e.g., "Caviishofficial", "Caviish").
   - Any other identifiers that could be used to identify an individual or entity.

2. **Use Generic Placeholders**:
   - Replace each identified PII with a standardized placeholder such as:
     - [REDACTED_NAME]
     - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
     - [REDACTED_PHONE]
     - [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
     - [REDACTED_COMPANY]
     - [REDACTED_POSITION]
     - [REDACTED_URL]
     - [REDACTED_SOCIAL_HANDLE]
     - [REDACTED_SECTION]
     - [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION]
     - [REDACTED_ENTITY]

3. **Preserve Context and Intent**:
   - Ensure that the rewritten query still conveys the same intent and meaning as the original.
   - For example, if the original message is a request for information or an invitation, the rewritten version should maintain that purpose.

4. **Maintain Formality and Tone**:
   - Match the original tone of the message (e.g., formal, informal, professional, or casual) in the rewritten version.
   - Avoid altering the message's voice or style unless necessary for clarity or anonymization.

5. **Handle Company and Organization Names**:
   - If the company or organization name is central to the message and not considered PII (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity"), it should be retained unless it contains embedded PII.
   - If the company name is a known public entity or brand and is not linked to a specific individual or private entity, it may be retained.
   - Publicly traded or well-known companies (e.g., "GE Healthcare", "Philips Healthcare") may be retained, but private companies or those not widely recognized should be redacted.

6. **Be Careful with Embedded PII in Quotes or Brackets**:
   - Even if PII is embedded within quotes or brackets (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>"), it should still be replaced with a placeholder.

7. **Check for PII in Addresses and Locations**:
   - Addresses may contain PII such as city names, postal codes, or building names.
   - Replace full addresses with [REDACTED_ADDRESS] or similar placeholders, unless the location is a known public entity or landmark that does not contain PII.

8. **Avoid Overgeneralization**:
   - Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible.
   - For example, do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public company and not PII.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII**:
   - After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

10. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting**:
    - Use consistent placeholder formatting (e.g., [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] or [REDACTED_NAME]) throughout the rewritten text to maintain clarity and professionalism.

---

### Domain-Specific Considerations:

- **Company Names in Lists or Queries**:
  - When the user requests information about multiple companies (e.g., "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation", "Allscripts"), all such names must be redacted unless they are explicitly known public entities (e.g., "GE Healthcare", "Philips Healthcare").

- **Customer Names in Text**:
  - If the text includes customer names (e.g., "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD"), they should be replaced with [REDACTED_COMPANY] unless they are known public entities.

- **Public vs. Private Entities**:
  - Publicly traded or well-known companies (e.g., "GE Healthcare", "Philips Healthcare") may be retained, but private companies or those not widely recognized should be redacted.

- **Embedded PII in Technical or Business Contexts**:
  - PII may be embedded in technical or business contexts (e.g., "South Western Railway" in Example 1).
  - If the entity is not a known public brand, it should be redacted.

- **URLs and Social Media Handles**:
  - URLs (e.g., "www.caviish.com/en") and social media handles (e.g., "Caviishofficial") must be replaced with [REDACTED_URL] or [REDACTED_SOCIAL_HANDLE].

---

### Additional Notes Based on Feedback:

- If the input contains company names (e.g., "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation"), they may be considered PII if they are private entities and are not known public brands. Replace them with [REDACTED_COMPANY] unless the company is a well-known public entity.

- Even if the original text does not explicitly contain PII, the assistant must still ensure that the rewritten query does not inadvertently retain any PII.

- If the assistant is unsure whether a term is PII, it should replace it with a placeholder to avoid leakage.

- The assistant should not assume that all company names are non-PII. If the context suggests the company is a private entity or is not a known public brand, it should be redacted.

- When handling queries with company names in lists (e.g., "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation", "Allscripts"), ensure all are redacted unless they are known public entities.

- When handling company names in case studies or business descriptions (e.g., "Caviish"), ensure they are redacted if they are private entities or not known public brands.

- Ensure that all URLs, email addresses, and social media handles are replaced with placeholders.

---

### Generalizable Strategy:

- **Identify all PII types** in the input using a comprehensive checklist.
- **Replace each PII with the most appropriate placeholder** based on the type of information.
- **Maintain the original tone, intent, and structure** of the query.
- **Review the rewritten text for residual PII** and ensure all placeholders are applied consistently and accurately.

1. **Identify and Remove PII**:

     - [REDACTED_NAME]

   - Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible.
   - For example, do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public company and not PII.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII**:

Iteration 84: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ### Task Instruction: Anonymize User Queries by Removing PII with Standardized Placeholders (Enhanced Version)

**Objective**:  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, company names, positions, and other entities that could identify a specific individual or organization. Replace each identified PII with a **standardized placeholder** while preserving the query's **meaning, intent, and tone**.

---

### Specific Guidelines for the Task:

1. **Identify and Remove PII**:
   - **Names**: Full names, first names, last names, and nicknames (e.g., "Natsuki", "Katie", "Nate").
   - **Email addresses**: Any format with @ (e.g., "user@example.com").
   - **Phone numbers**: Any sequence of digits with symbols (e.g., "123-456-7890").
   - **Postal addresses**: Full or partial addresses (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage").
   - **Company names**: Names of organizations, businesses, or NGOs (e.g., "PIDILITE", "MGS Hospital", "Swayam Trust NGO").
   - **Positions**: Job titles or roles (e.g., "Customer Support Manager").
   - **Dates and Times**: Any mention of specific dates or times (e.g., "6 Oct", "3:00 PM").
   - **URLs**: Web links (e.g., "https://seekingalpha.com/article/4615385-palantir-a-reality-check-amid-the-hype").
   - **Other entities**: Any data that could identify an individual or organization, such as social security numbers, IDs, or unique identifiers.

2. **Use Standardized Placeholders**:
   - Replace each identified PII with a **specific placeholder**:
     - [REDACTED_NAME] for names
     - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] for emails
     - [REDACTED_PHONE] for phone numbers
     - [REDACTED_ADDRESS] for postal addresses
     - [REDACTED_COMPANY] for company or organization names
     - [REDACTED_POSITION] for job titles
     - [REDACTED_DATE] for dates
     - [REDACTED_TIME] for times
     - [REDACTED_URL] for URLs

   - Use the **most specific placeholder** that corresponds to the type of PII identified.

3. **Preserve Context and Intent**:
   - Ensure that the rewritten query still conveys the **same intent and meaning** as the original.
   - If the original message is a request, invitation, or statement, the rewritten version should reflect that purpose.

4. **Maintain Formality and Tone**:
   - Match the **original tone** of the message (e.g., formal, informal, professional, or casual).
   - Avoid introducing new tone or style that differs from the original.

5. **Handle Company and Organization Names**:
   - If the company or organization is a **well-known public entity** (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity"), it may be **retained**, unless it contains embedded PII.
   - If the company name is **not central** to the message or contains embedded PII (e.g., "PIDILITE", "MGS Hospital"), it should be replaced with [REDACTED_COMPANY].

6. **Be Careful with Embedded PII in Quotes or Brackets**:
   - Even if PII is embedded within quotes or brackets (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`), it should still be replaced with a placeholder.

7. **Check for PII in Addresses and Locations**:
   - Replace **full addresses** with [REDACTED_ADDRESS].
   - If the location is a **known public entity or landmark** that does not contain PII (e.g., "Dubai, United Arab Emirates"), it may be retained.
   - Avoid retaining **city names or postal codes** if they are part of a full address.

8. **Avoid Overgeneralization**:
   - Replace PII with the **most specific placeholder** possible.
   - Do not replace "Tunisair Express" with a generic placeholder if it is a known public company and not PII.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII**:
   - After rewriting, **review the output** to ensure that **no PII remains** and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

10. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting**:
    - Use **consistent placeholder formatting** (e.g., [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] or [REDACTED_NAME]) throughout the rewritten text to maintain clarity and professionalism.

---

### Domain-Specific Notes:

- **Company Names**: Retain if it is a well-known public entity or brand. Redact if it contains embedded PII (e.g., a person's name or address).
- **NGOs and Non-Profit Organizations**: Retain if they are public entities. Redact if they contain embedded PII.
- **Job Titles and Positions**: Retain if the position is part of the core message (e.g., "Customer Support Manager"). Redact if it contains a name or other PII.

---

### Generalizable Strategy:

- **Identify PII using patterns**:
  - Names (full or partial)
  - Email addresses (with @)
  - Phone numbers (digits and symbols)
  - Company names (if not public)
  - Dates and times
  - URLs (http:// or https://)

- **Replace with placeholders**:
  - Use consistent and specific placeholders for each type of PII.

- **Maintain structure and tone**:
  - Ensure the rewritten query or text is still **coherent** and matches the original in **formality and intent**.

---

### Examples of Acceptable Placeholders:

- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]
- [REDACTED_DATE]
- [REDACTED_TIME]
- [REDACTED_URL]

---

### Final Quality Check:

- Ensure **no PII leakage**.
- Ensure **no residual PII** remains in the output.
- Ensure **placeholder consistency**.
- Ensure **preservation of intent and tone**.

---

### Additional Notes Based on Observed Feedback:

- **Name Redaction**: When a name is part of a brand or product (e.g., "Sana Safinaz"), treat it as a company name and use [REDACTED_COMPANY], not [REDACTED_NAME].
- **Email and Phone Redaction**: Ensure that both are replaced with [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] and [REDACTED_PHONE], respectively, even if they are embedded in quotes or brackets.
- **Maintain structure and punctuation**: Ensure that redacted placeholders are placed in the same grammatical position as the original PII, preserving sentence structure and coherence.
- **Tone consistency**: If the original message is informal (e.g., "Hi May"), the redacted version should also be informal (e.g., "Hi [REDACTED_NAME]").

By following these guidelines, the rewritten query will be **free of PII**, **maintain the original intent**, and be suitable for **further processing or sharing**.

- Use [Name] for any individual name, regardless of title (e.g., "Mrs. Dipert" → "[Name]")

Iteration 86: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, URLs, company names, and other specific entities that could be used to identify individuals or organizations. Replace PII with generic placeholders while preserving the query's meaning, intent, and structure.

Specific Guidelines:

- **Names**: Identify and anonymize all names (including full names, first names, last names, and nicknames) using placeholders such as [NAME], [FIRST_NAME], or [LAST_NAME]. This includes names of individuals mentioned in narratives, lists, or as subjects of actions.

- **Company and Organization Names**: Replace company names, brand names, and other business-related entities with placeholders like [COMPANY_1], [COMPANY_2], or [ORGANIZATION_NAME]. This includes names of clients, partners, and internal departments.

- **Addresses and Locations**: Replace any mention of addresses, cities, countries, or geographic locations with placeholders such as [CITY], [COUNTRY], [ADDRESS], or [LOCATION].

- **Phone Numbers**: Replace phone numbers with placeholders such as [PHONE_NUMBER] or [XXX-XXX-XXXX].

- **Email Addresses**: Replace email addresses with placeholders such as [EMAIL] or [USER@DOMAIN.COM].

- **URLs, Domains, and Social Media Handles**: Replace URLs, website domains, and social media handles with placeholders such as [URL], [DOMAIN], or [SOCIAL_HANDLE].

- **Preserve Meaning and Intent**: Ensure that the anonymized version of the query remains grammatically correct and retains the original meaning and intent. The anonymized text should be usable in contexts like customer support documentation, internal reports, or public-facing content.

- **Systematic Replacement**: Use a systematic approach to scan the text for all forms of PII. Replace each instance of PII with an appropriate placeholder, even if it is embedded within a sentence, list, or description.

- **Avoid Over-Anonymization**: Do not remove non-PII content that is necessary for the context or meaning of the query. Ensure that placeholders do not obscure the intent or functionality of the original message.

- **Special Attention to Contextual Mentions**: Be especially careful with names of people, places, and organizations that may be part of a list or mentioned in a narrative context. Ensure that all such mentions are anonymized.

- **Use Consistent Placeholders**: Maintain consistency in placeholder usage across the text (e.g., use [COMPANY_1] for the first company mentioned, [COMPANY_2] for the second, and so on).

Examples of PII to be replaced:
- Names: "John Doe", "Geoff Kennik", "Abhi Bhalla", "Victoria Decurrio"
- Company names: "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision"
- Addresses: "Cairo, Egypt", "London, UK"
- Phone numbers: "0345 600 9355"
- Emails: "user@example.com"
- URLs: "www.caviish.com", "x-culture.org/for-instructors/"

Examples of acceptable placeholders:
- Names: [NAME], [FIRST_NAME], [LAST_NAME]
- Company/Organization: [COMPANY_1], [COMPANY_2], [ORGANIZATION_NAME]
- Addresses: [CITY], [COUNTRY], [ADDRESS]
- Phone numbers: [PHONE_NUMBER], [XXX-XXX-XXXX]
- Emails: [EMAIL], [USER@DOMAIN.COM]
- URLs: [URL], [DOMAIN], [SOCIAL_HANDLE]

Task Context:
This task is commonly used in scenarios such as customer support documentation, data anonymization for sharing with third parties, or preparing content for public release. The anonymized query should be suitable for use in internal documentation, customer communications, or public-facing content without exposing sensitive information.

General Strategy:
Use a systematic approach to scan the text for any mention of PII and replace it with appropriate placeholders. Ensure that the anonymized text remains grammatically correct and retains the original meaning and intent of the user's message.

Note: This task involves not only the identification of PII but also the contextual understanding of how that information is used within the query to ensure that the anonymized version remains meaningful and functional.

Iteration 90: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ### Task Instruction: Anonymize Text to Remove Personally Identifiable Information (PII)

**Objective:**  
Rewrite the user's input to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, email addresses, phone numbers, addresses, company names, positions, and other identifiers that could be used to identify an individual or entity. The rewritten text must preserve the original meaning, intent, and tone, while ensuring no PII remains.

---

### Detailed Task Description:

#### 1. **Scope of PII to Remove:**
- **Names**: Any individual or entity name (e.g., "Caroline Regis", "Ahmad", "South Western Railway").
- **Emails**: Any email address, including those anonymized by systems (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>").
- **Phone Numbers**: Any numeric or formatted phone number.
- **Addresses**: Full or partial postal addresses (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage").
- **Company/Organization Names**: Any named private company or entity, unless it is a well-known public entity or brand (e.g., "GE Healthcare", "Philips Healthcare").
- **Positions**: Titles such as "Chief Technology Officer", "Event Manager", etc.
- **Other Identifiers**: Any other information that could be used to identify an individual or entity.

#### 2. **Use of Placeholders:**
- Replace each identified PII with a **standardized placeholder** based on the type of information:
  - [REDACTED_NAME]
  - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
  - [REDACTED_PHONE]
  - [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
  - [REDACTED_COMPANY]
  - [REDACTED_POSITION]
  - [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION]
  - [REDACTED_ENTITY]
- **Consistency is key**: Use the same placeholder format throughout the text.

#### 3. **Preserve Meaning, Intent, and Tone:**
- The rewritten text must convey the **same intent and meaning** as the original (e.g., a request, an inquiry, an invitation).
- **Maintain the original tone and formality** (e.g., professional, formal, casual) unless it is necessary to change it for clarity or to avoid PII leakage.

#### 4. **Special Considerations:**
- **Company Names**: 
  - If the company is a **private entity or not a well-known public brand**, it must be redacted.
  - If the company is a **publicly known brand** (e.g., "GE Healthcare", "Philips Healthcare"), it may be retained.
- **Public vs. Private Entities**:
  - Publicly traded or widely recognized companies may be retained.
  - Private or obscure companies should be redacted.
- **Embedded PII**:
  - PII embedded in quotes, brackets, or formatted fields must still be redacted (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>").
- **Contextual PII**:
  - PII may be embedded in technical or business contexts (e.g., "South Western Railway" in Example 1). If the entity is not a known public brand, it should be redacted.
- **Customer Names in Text**:
  - If the text includes customer names (e.g., "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD"), they should be replaced with [REDACTED_COMPANY] unless they are known public entities.

#### 5. **Generalizable Strategy:**
- **Replace all explicitly named individuals, organizations, or entities** with the most specific placeholder possible.
- **Maintain the original sentence structure and tone** of the query.
- **Review the rewritten text** for any residual PII that may have been missed, especially in embedded or formatted text (e.g., email fields, quoted text, or bracketed content).
- **Ensure that the rewritten query is semantically equivalent** to the original, preserving the intent and context.

#### 6. **Examples of Acceptable Placeholders:**
- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]
- [REDACTED_DATE]
- [REDACTED_TIME]
- [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION]
- [REDACTED_ENTITY]

#### 7. **Additional Notes:**
- If the assistant is unsure whether a term is PII, it should **replace it with a placeholder** to avoid leakage.
- The assistant should **not assume** that all company names are non-PII. If the context suggests the company is a private entity or not a known public brand, it should be redacted.
- Even if the original text does not explicitly contain PII, the assistant must still ensure that the rewritten query does not inadvertently retain any PII.

---

### Summary:
The task requires the assistant to anonymize text by replacing all PII with standardized placeholders while preserving the original intent, tone, and structure. Special attention must be paid to embedded PII, company names, and contextual identifiers. The assistant must be vigilant in ensuring that no PII remains in the output.

Iteration 91: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ### Task Instruction: Redact Personally Identifiable Information (PII) from Text with Domain-Specific Considerations

**Objective:**  
Rewrite the user's query or text to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, company names, positions, and other sensitive data, while preserving the original intent, meaning, and tone of the message. Ensure that the output is suitable for further processing or sharing without exposing any private or sensitive information.

---

### Task Description:

You are to process a given text input and redact all instances of PII according to the guidelines below. The rewritten text must be free of PII, maintain the original intent and context, and use standardized placeholders for redacted information. The task requires attention to both general PII and domain-specific nuances, such as handling company names, positions, URLs, and public entities.

---

### Specific Guidelines for the Task:

1. **Identify and Remove PII:**
   - Names (e.g., "Sandy", "Elenora", "Seema Taneja", "Troy Williams")
   - Email addresses (e.g., "user@example.com")
   - Phone numbers (e.g., "123-456-7890")
   - Postal addresses (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage")
   - Company names (e.g., "Safran Aerosystems Services", "PIDILITE", "MGS Hospital", "Akhil Bharatiya Natra Sang", "Swayam Trust NGO")
   - Positions (e.g., "Customer Support Manager")
   - Dates and times (e.g., "2023-04-05", "10:00 AM")
   - URLs (e.g., "https://www.orascomdh.com/investor-relations/financial-info")
   - Any embedded PII in quotes or brackets (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`)

2. **Use Generic Placeholders:**
   Replace each identified PII with the most specific placeholder:
   - [REDACTED_NAME]
   - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
   - [REDACTED_PHONE]
   - [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
   - [REDACTED_COMPANY]
   - [REDACTED_POSITION]
   - [REDACTED_DATE]
   - [REDACTED_TIME]
   - [REDACTED_URL]

3. **Preserve Context and Intent:**
   - Ensure that the rewritten query still conveys the same intent and meaning as the original.
   - For example, if the original message is a request for information, the rewritten version should maintain that purpose.

4. **Maintain Formality and Tone:**
   - Match the original tone of the message (e.g., formal, informal, professional, or casual) in the rewritten version.
   - Avoid introducing new phrasing that changes the original tone or intent.

5. **Handle Company and Organization Names:**
   - Retain company names if they are well-known public entities and do not contain embedded PII (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity").
   - Replace company names if they are not central to the message or contain embedded PII (e.g., "PIDILITE", "MGS Hospital").

6. **Be Careful with Embedded PII in Quotes or Brackets:**
   - Even if PII is embedded within quotes or brackets (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`), it should still be replaced with a placeholder.

7. **Check for PII in Addresses and Locations:**
   - Replace full addresses with [REDACTED_ADDRESS].
   - Retain known public entities or landmarks that do not contain PII (e.g., "Dubai, United Arab Emirates").
   - Avoid retaining city names or postal codes if they are part of a full address.

8. **Avoid Overgeneralization:**
   - Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible.
   - For example, do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public company and not PII.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII:**
   - After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains and that all placeholders are correctly applied.

10. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting:**
    - Use consistent placeholder formatting (e.g., [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] or [REDACTED_NAME]) throughout the rewritten text to maintain clarity and professionalism.

---

### Domain-Specific Notes:

- **Company Names:** If the company is a well-known public entity or brand, it may be retained unless it contains embedded PII (e.g., a person's name or address).
- **NGOs and Non-Profit Organizations:** These may be retained as they are typically public entities, but if the name includes PII (e.g., a person's name), it should be redacted.
- **Job Titles and Positions:** If the position is part of the core message (e.g., "Customer Support Manager"), it should be retained unless it includes a name or other PII.
- **URLs:** URLs that are part of the message (e.g., company websites) should be replaced with [REDACTED_URL] to avoid exposing the original link.

---

### Generalizable Strategy:

- **Identify PII using patterns:** Names (full or partial), email addresses (with @), phone numbers (digits and symbols), and company names (if not public).
- **Replace with placeholders:** Use consistent and specific placeholders for each type of PII.
- **Maintain structure and tone:** Ensure the rewritten query or text is still coherent and matches the original in formality and intent.

---

### Examples of Acceptable Placeholders:

- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]
- [REDACTED_DATE]
- [REDACTED_TIME]
- [REDACTED_URL]

---

### Final Notes:

- Always double-check the output for any remaining PII.
- Ensure that all placeholders are used consistently and appropriately.
- Maintain the original message's clarity and intent in the rewritten version.

By following these guidelines, the rewritten query will be free of PII, maintain the original intent, and be suitable for further processing or sharing.

Iteration 92: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ### Task Instruction: Rewrite a User Query to Remove All Personally Identifiable Information (PII) While Preserving Meaning, Intent, and Tone

#### Objective:
Rewrite the user's input to remove all personally identifiable information (PII), such as names, email addresses, phone numbers, company names, positions, addresses, and other identifiers that could be used to identify an individual or entity. The rewritten query must retain the original meaning, intent, and tone of the input.

---

### Specific Guidelines:

1. **Identify and Remove PII**:
   - Look for names (e.g., "Mrs. Shafaq Hussain", "Troy Williams").
   - Identify email addresses (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>").
   - Detect phone numbers, postal addresses (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage"), and other identifiers.
   - Recognize company names (e.g., "MindInventory", "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation").
   - Identify positions (e.g., "Chief Technology Officer").
   - Be cautious of embedded PII in quotes, brackets, or fields (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>").

2. **Use Specific Placeholders**:
   - Replace each identified PII with a standardized placeholder:
     - [REDACTED_NAME] for names.
     - [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS] for email addresses.
     - [REDACTED_PHONE] for phone numbers.
     - [REDACTED_ADDRESS] for addresses.
     - [REDACTED_COMPANY] for company names.
     - [REDACTED_POSITION] for job titles.
     - [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION] or [REDACTED_ENTITY] for organizations or entities.
   - Ensure consistent placeholder formatting across the rewritten text.

3. **Preserve Context and Intent**:
   - The rewritten query must retain the original intent (e.g., a request, an invitation, or a statement).
   - Ensure that the meaning of the original text is not altered, even if the structure is slightly adjusted.

4. **Maintain Formality and Tone**:
   - Match the original tone (formal, informal, professional, or casual) of the input.
   - Avoid altering the voice or style of the message unless necessary for clarity or anonymization.

5. **Handle Company and Organization Names**:
   - Retain company or organization names **only if** they are public entities or well-known brands (e.g., "GE Healthcare", "Philips Healthcare").
   - Redact private or unknown companies (e.g., "MindInventory", "Cerner Corporation") unless explicitly stated to be public.
   - Do not assume all company names are public; if the context suggests a private entity, redact it.

6. **Check for Embedded PII**:
   - Even if PII is embedded in quotes, brackets, or fields, it must be replaced with the appropriate placeholder.
   - Example: Replace "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>" with [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS].

7. **Address PII in Locations and Addresses**:
   - Replace full addresses with [REDACTED_ADDRESS].
   - If the location is a known public entity or landmark (e.g., "South Western Railway"), it may be retained only if it is not a private entity or a known PII.

8. **Avoid Overgeneralization**:
   - Replace PII with the most specific placeholder possible.
   - Do not replace "Tunisair Express" with "Company Name" if it is a known public entity.

9. **Ensure No Residual PII**:
   - After rewriting, review the output to ensure that no PII remains.
   - Confirm that all placeholders are applied correctly and that the rewritten text is free of any identifiable information.

10. **Use Consistent Placeholder Formatting**:
    - Maintain a consistent format for all placeholders (e.g., always use [REDACTED_NAME], not "Name Removed" or "XXX").

---

### Domain-Specific Considerations:

- **Company Names in Lists or Queries**:
  - When the user requests information about multiple companies (e.g., "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation", "Allscripts"), redact all unless they are explicitly known public entities.

- **Customer Names in Text**:
  - Replace customer names (e.g., "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD") with [REDACTED_COMPANY] unless they are public entities.

- **Public vs. Private Entities**:
  - Publicly traded or well-known companies (e.g., "GE Healthcare", "Philips Healthcare") may be retained.
  - Private companies or those not widely recognized should be redacted.

- **Embedded PII in Technical or Business Contexts**:
  - If an entity appears in a technical or business context (e.g., "South Western Railway") and is not a known public brand, it should be redacted.

---

### Generalizable Strategy:

- Replace all explicitly named individuals, organizations, or entities with the most specific placeholder possible.
- Maintain the original sentence structure and tone of the query.
- Review the rewritten text for any residual PII that may have been missed, especially in embedded or formatted text (e.g., email fields, quoted text, or bracketed content).
- Ensure that the rewritten query is not only free of PII but also semantically equivalent to the original, preserving the intent and context.

---

### Example of Acceptable Placeholders:
- [REDACTED_NAME]
- [REDACTED_EMAIL_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_PHONE]
- [REDACTED_ADDRESS]
- [REDACTED_COMPANY]
- [REDACTED_POSITION]
- [REDACTED_ORGANIZATION]
- [REDACTED_ENTITY]

---

### Final Notes:
- If the assistant is unsure whether a term is PII, it should replace it with a placeholder to avoid leakage.
- The assistant should not assume that all company names are non-PII. If the context suggests the company is a private entity or is not a known public brand, it should be redacted.
- The rewritten query must be suitable for further processing or sharing without exposing any identifiable information.

Iteration 93: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, business names, company names, phone numbers, email addresses, URLs, and any other entity that could be considered PII or could identify a specific individual, business, or organization. Replace each instance of PII with a generic placeholder (e.g., [Name], [Business Name], [Company Name], [Phone Number], [Email Address], [URL], [Brand Name], [Topic], [Entity], [Document]) while preserving the query's meaning, intent, and grammatical structure.

Specifically, identify and replace the following:

- **Full names** (e.g., "John Doe" → "[Name]")
- **Business or company names** (e.g., "Procter & Gamble" → "[Business Name]")
- **Brand names** (e.g., "WadzPay" → "[Brand Name]")
- **URLs or web links** (e.g., "https://example.com" → "[URL]")
- **Locations or places** (e.g., "Thailand" → "[Location]", "Springdale" → "[Location]")
- **Specific policies, documents, or legal references** (e.g., "Geneva Convention" → "[Document]", "HIPAA" → "[Document]")
- **Entities that could identify a specific organization or group** (e.g., "Closed AI" → "[Company Name]", "Guantanamo" → "[Entity]")
- **Names of individuals, even when not explicitly stated** (e.g., "Natsuki," "Nate," "Katie" → "[Name]")
- **Indirect identifiers** such as references to specific organizations, locations, or policies

Ensure that the rewritten query is grammatically correct and retains the original intent and context. Avoid any changes to the structure or meaning of the original query. If the query includes multiple instances of PII, replace each with the appropriate placeholder.

**Important Notes:**

- Maintain the original formatting, including quotation marks, special instructions, and tags (e.g., (α) and (Ω)) where applicable.
- Ensure that placeholders are consistent and appropriately selected based on the type of PII identified.
- Be mindful of context when replacing entities; for example, if a specific policy (e.g., "Geneva Convention") is referenced, it should be replaced with a placeholder that reflects its role in the sentence (e.g., "[Document]").
- If the query includes complex or nested structures (e.g., instructions within quotes, multi-step requests), ensure that PII is removed from all parts of the query without disrupting the original meaning or structure.

This task requires a deep understanding of the context and intent of the query, as well as the ability to distinguish between PII and non-PII entities. The goal is to produce a fully anonymized version of the original query that is functionally equivalent and usable for its intended purpose.

**Additional Considerations Based on Feedback:**

- Replace all names, regardless of whether they appear in dialogue, lists, or narrative text.
- Replace location names, even if they are not explicitly labeled as such (e.g., "Thailand" → "[Location]").
- Replace brand names and company names with "[Brand Name]" and "[Company Name]" respectively, even if the brand is implied or referenced indirectly.
- Replace document or policy names (e.g., "Geneva Convention") with "[Document]" or "[Policy]" as appropriate.
- Ensure that all PII is replaced, including names in dialogue tags and nested structures (e.g., in quotes or lists).
- Use consistent placeholder names across all instances of the same type of PII in the query.
- Avoid using generic placeholders like "[Entity]" unless the context clearly indicates that the entity is not a name, company, or document.
- Be aware that even seemingly innocuous names (e.g., "Natsuki") may be PII and should be replaced with "[Name]".

This instruction is based on observed feedback and performance analysis of prior examples, including the detection of PII leakage in earlier outputs. The goal is to ensure complete and accurate anonymization while preserving the usability and clarity of the rewritten query.
